docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:45:Here is what Gate A runs, all for zero GPU dollars. The whole orchestration runs for real. The only thing faked is the network call to each model. We do this through one clean seam: an injectable per-role client. In the real product, that client talks to the real model endpoints. In the dry run, that same client replays recorded responses from fixture files, keyed to each claim. The dispatch code never knows it is being mocked; the mock is injected from outside. This is the single hard build rule, because if the fake lived any higher up, say faking "run the whole Mirror pass," the dry run would prove nothing about how the machine dispatches and flows. The fake must sit at the model-call boundary and nowhere higher.
docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:47:Around those faked model calls, everything else is real and exercised end to end. The role dispatch and ordering are real. The per-claim Mirror-then-Sentinel-then-Judge flow is real. The deterministic Python sentence check is real. The release routing is real. The memory write of verified claims is real, on fixtures. The pause and resume is real, on fixtures. Retrieval runs as a couple of single cheap real probes, not a full sweep. And the Generator runs for real and cheap, because it is the one model with a live endpoint. No full-power sweep fires in the dry run; that is strictly after the money gate.
docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:49:Now, what does green Gate A actually mean. It means every one of these checks passed. The unit and fixture test suites all pass. The lock-consistency checker exits clean, confirming the model slugs and roles in code match the lock. The offline preflight returns clean. The role-dispatch returns exactly four pins, generator, mirror, sentinel, and judge, where today it returns only two. The coverage gate accepts all four pins, tested against a fixture copy of the lock flipped to the locked state, because the real lock is not signed yet. The Sentinel polarity test confirms yes maps to ungrounded and no maps to grounded; an inverted mapping fails the gate. The Judge parser confirms it returns exactly one of the five verdicts. The Mirror two-pass parses, with the citation pass and the separate verdict pass both working. The release routing is correct: a fabricated claim gates the run on occurrence, an unsupported claim gets one rewrite then gates only on thin residual coverage. The completeness check confirms all four roles actually appear in the captured calls. The pause-and-resume integrity holds under crash injection: we kill the run at every checkpoint boundary and confirm the Generator never re-bills, verdicts replay from the cursor, nothing double-writes, and a drifted protocol fingerprint fails the resume closed. The memory write discipline holds: only verified and partial claims enter, fabricated and unreachable never do, the write is idempotent so re-running never double-counts, and the write fails loudly when the store is missing. The cross-time contradiction check fires correctly against a pre-loaded prior. And the three cheap real probes succeed: one search call, one Semantic Scholar call, one tiny Generator generation, each returning real output from a model whose served identity matches the pin.
docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:59:The planted traps cover the cases that matter. A genuine fabrication with no supporting span: the harness must flag it ungrounded, judge it fabricated, refuse it in place, gate the run, and keep it out of memory. A claim whose numbers do not match its span: dropped by the Python check or judged unsupported, with a recorded gap. A clean verified claim: kept in the prose and written to memory only at the provisional tier, never straight to durable. A partial claim on a high-severity topic: one clarify attempt, then a visible advisory marker. A missing must-cover item, like an absent contraindication: the run is gated even though overall coverage looks fine. A citation that points at a source that does not exist: escalated to the fabricated gate. A claim that contradicts a seeded prior in memory: the contradiction is recorded. And a provisional, not-yet-audited memory claim: confirmed it can never feed back into grounding, which is the firewall.
docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:73:There is one economic lever sitting just below the architecture, and I will name it rather than silently pick it. The feasibility work recommends serving the Mirror through Cohere's own Canadian managed endpoint at full precision, which would shrink the unavoidable GPU rental down to just the small Sentinel model. The flow is identical either way, so this is a serving choice, not an architecture change. But it changes the dry-run economics, so it is flagged for the operator to decide on the lock-change issue. The binding decision today still routes both Mirror and Sentinel to rented GPUs.
docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:83:Fourth, entity resolution. If the machine fails to recognize that tirzepatide, Mounjaro, and the lab code are the same drug, it silently splits one entity into two and the cross-time contradiction is never caught. Is a deterministic sovereign drug-and-condition ontology mirror the right dependency?

docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:22:**Gap two — pausable and resumable.** What works today is cancel, not pause. The production run store at `src/polaris_v6/queue/run_store.py` can move a run to cancelled, and the main sweep script honors a cancel request at stage boundaries. There is no paused state and no real resume in that path. Separately, a capable pause-resume state machine does exist in `src/polaris_graph/audit_ir/job_queue.py`, with pause, resume, and checkpoint methods, plus working pause and resume web endpoints. But here is the catch: the real production runner explicitly refuses to pause — it throws an error saying pause is not supported and tells you to cancel and re-run from scratch. And resume, even where it exists, just re-runs the job from step zero, because no runner ever reads back the saved checkpoint state. There is also a third, genuinely capable any-stage rewind engine in `src/polaris_graph/checkpoint_manager.py`, but it is switched off by default and its checkpoint database is an empty 3-byte file — it has never saved a single checkpoint, and it sits on a pipeline that the production sweep does not use. The gap is large. The one main thing to do: make the deployed pipeline save its full intermediate state at each stage boundary, then teach the runner to read that state and skip already-done stages on resume. This is exactly the open, unstarted GitHub issue #629.

docs\polaris_step_b_full_set_audit_2026_05_27.md:93:1. **Highest open-weight recall** at AA-Omniscience Accuracy 43.3% — second is V4 Flash 37.2%. docs\polaris_step_b_full_set_audit_2026_05_27.md:148:1. **Highest published calibration of any frontier-comparable open-weight model.** AA-Omniscience Non-Hallucination 86%, rank 1, ~3pp ahead of next-best (per Artificial Analysis 2026-05-20 review). docs\polaris_step_b_full_set_audit_2026_05_27.md:195:These are different tasks; conflating them produces miscalibrated picks. docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:21:**Pivot recommendation for the 9-day window: do NOT rip out the regex+atom stack. Bolt on three things, in this order:** (1) **Vectara HHEM-2.1-Open** (0.1B params, Apache-2.0, ~0.6s/section on RTX 3090, self-hostable, catches negation correctly — see §3.2) as a per-section faithfulness gate post-strict-verify; (2) **Patronus Lynx 8B** (open source, MIT/Llama-3 license, beats GPT-4o on PubMedQA by 8.3%, returns JSON `{REASONING, SCORE: PASS|FAIL}`) as a per-section LLM-judge gate; (3) Keep the current atom system as the **generation-time scaffold** but stop treating it as the verification layer — it's the prompt-design layer. Codex's §-1.1 line-by-line audit becomes the gold-standard third gate (already in place). Demo-ready by 2026-06-02 with ~400 lines of plumbing, no architecture rip-out.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:31:1. **Prompt-level atom injection.** V4 Pro (DeepSeek's reasoning model) is prompted to emit per-claim `atom_NNN` tokens inline with the generated text, plus `[ev_XXX]` evidence-block citations. The atom catalogue is pre-extracted from corpus markdown tables (per-cell percentages, e.g. `atom_007 = {endpoint: constipation, arm: TZP_15mg, value: 7.1%}`) via `src/polaris_graph/generator/claim_atom_extractor.py`. Approach is "Approach C hybrid" per Codex APPROVE_DESIGN 2026-05-26 — prompt-side instruction plus post-hoc enforcement.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:33:2. **Regex-based quantitative-claim detection.** `src/polaris_graph/generator/atom_refusal_validator.py` runs Trigger A (number + endpoint vocab, ~80 endpoint terms) and Trigger B (number alone with exclusions). Sentences flagged as REQUIRES_ATOM that lack a valid `atom_NNN` are replaced with refusal templates. The file currently has ~20 regex patterns covering trial-design exemptions, eligibility-range patterns, and a-f branches for result-attribution language. Iter-4 design decision (post-Codex iter-3 audit) was to **drop eligibility-range disambiguation** because pure-regex disambiguation between "eligibility framing + endpoint+number" and "outcome claim + baseline mention" is fundamentally fragile.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:37:**What the architecture does NOT do.** It does not run entailment checks (no NLI head on claim×evidence pair). It does not run LLM-as-judge faithfulness per sentence (Codex provides this manually, externally, per §-1.1, but not inline). It does not detect qualitative-negation mismatches — a sentence "Constipation did not lead to discontinuation" passes Trigger A (no number) and Trigger B (no number), shares enough content words with the evidence span to clear strict-verify, and the regex has no semantic model of "did not" vs "did at 0.2-0.4%". This is the gap.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:53:**Can it catch the constipation fabrication?** Yes — if Claude is asked "does this sentence about constipation match the table data?", Claude with Citations will return either a cited span that confirms the claim or no citation block (which the consumer code can treat as unsupported). But this is essentially "LLM-as-judge with byte-accurate quotes," which is option 3.7 with US-vendor caveats.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:85:**Verdict.** **Second top recommendation.** Run as a per-section LLM-judge gate after HHEM. Two gates catch different failure modes — HHEM catches per-sentence contradiction, Lynx catches per-answer-block reasoning failures.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:89:**What they do.** Eval frameworks, not runtime gates. RAGAS provides Faithfulness (claim-level grounding), Answer Relevancy, Context Precision, Context Recall metrics via LLM-as-judge wrappers [^ragas_2026]. The faithfulness metric **measures the proportion of statements in the answer that are grounded in retrieved content — a 0.6 score means roughly 40% of statements are not grounded, which is hallucination in the strictest technical sense** [^ragas_2026].
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:91:**Pain point in production.** RAGAS has a known bug where **NaN scores appear when the LLM judge returns invalid JSON during metric calculation; there is no graceful fallback, so a single bad API response can fail an entire eval run** [^ragas_2026]. This is a deal-breaker for runtime gating but acceptable for offline benchmarking.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:93:**Sovereignty fit.** Depends on judge model. RAGAS supports any OpenAI-compatible endpoint, so pointing it at a self-hosted Llama / Qwen / DeepSeek inference is straightforward. The framework itself is MIT.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:115:**MedScore (the medical-specific decomposition).** Specifically designed for medical free-form text. Achieves **74.4% valid-claim rate on AskDocsAI vs FActScore's 17%**, reduces unverifiable claims from 37.3% to 9.3% [^medscore_2025]. **However: it uses closed-source models (GPT-4o, GPT-4o-mini) for decomposition** — sovereignty incompatible. Could be re-implemented with a local Qwen3 / DeepSeek-distilled judge.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:135:### 3.8 LLM-as-judge with grounded reasoning
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:137:**What it does.** Use a strong LLM (Claude Opus 4.7, GPT-5, Gemini 2.5 Pro, Llama 3.3 70B) as a judge, prompted to do per-claim faithfulness verification with quoted evidence. Datadog's 2025 engineering blog and Patronus's research both validate this as the highest-quality detection method when no fine-tuned alternative exists [^datadog_judge_2025]. Lynx (§3.3) is the open-source instantiation of this pattern, pre-trained for it.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:139:**Production caveat.** Latency 2-10s per call depending on judge model. Cost rises linearly with output length. Acceptable for offline benchmarking, marginal for runtime gating unless the judge is small (Lynx 8B is the sweet spot).
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:141:**Sovereignty fit.** Depends on judge. Qwen3 / DeepSeek-distilled / Llama 3.3 are sovereignty-compatible. GPT-5 / Claude / Gemini are not (US vendors).
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:143:**Verdict.** **Lynx 8B is the right embodiment** (see §3.3). Don't reinvent the LLM-judge wheel with raw prompts when Lynx exists pre-trained on HaluBench.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:159:**The constipation fabrication test.** None of the three frontier DR products has a public report on whether they reliably catch the "X did not lead to discontinuation" class of fabrication. The Columbia Journalism Review citation-audit (cited above) suggests Perplexity's 37% citation hallucination rate would *probably* catch quantitative misalignment some of the time (citation links to wrong table cell), but qualitative-negation specifically is unmeasured. POLARIS's combination of atom-extraction + HHEM faithfulness gate + Lynx LLM-judge + Codex §-1.1 audit would, on present evidence, **outperform all three frontier DR products on qualitative-negation faithfulness — provided the demo doesn't ship with V4 Pro's 8.6% raw hallucination rate as the only line of defence**.
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:167:| Anthropic Citations | Generator-only — fails sovereignty | Yes (if used as judge) | **Fail** (US vendor) | Hybrid only; skip for demo |
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:169:| Patronus Lynx 8B/70B | Augments via LLM-judge layer | **Yes** (+8.3% on PubMedQA over GPT-4o) | **Pass** (Llama-3 community, self-host) | **2nd best, ~2 days** |
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:170:| RAGAS | No (eval framework, not gate) | Partial (LLM-judge dependent) | Pass (judge-dependent) | Offline benchmarking only |

docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:210:**Carney-pitch line.** "POLARIS combines four independent faithfulness layers — per-token atom grounding, per-sentence span verification, per-claim NLI entailment (HHEM-2.1), and per-section LLM-judge reasoning (Patronus Lynx) — beating the public hallucination rates of every frontier deep-research product on the Vectara leaderboard and matching GPT-4o-class detection on PubMedQA medical hallucination, fully self-hosted on Canadian / EU sovereign infrastructure."
docs\clinical_rag_validation_sota_2026_05_26.md:216:Rip out atom_NNN, regex validator, strict-verify. docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:48:2. **No log-probability / information-theoretic anomaly detector across the generator ensemble.** This is the gap the CHECK paper [^check_paper] specifically addresses: hallucinations have **statistically distinct distribution shapes** (high entropy, high KL divergence across models in an ensemble) that are detectable without any retrieval. POLARIS's two-family invariant already requires two distinct LLM lineages — extending to 3-5 and computing entropy / KL across them is mechanical. **Fix:** re-implement CHECK's classifier on POLARIS's existing generator + a Qwen3 mirror + a Llama-3.3 mirror.
docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:52:4. **No clinical-database grounding layer separate from the per-document evidence pool.** POLARIS grounds against the corpus the operator provides per-run. CHECK grounds against a continuously-updated ClinicalTrials.gov-derived database (68k trials) maintained at BlueScrubs. The two are complementary: per-run corpus catches in-context contradictions; persistent database catches global contradictions (the "this drug isn't approved for that indication" class). **Fix:** ship a ClinicalTrials.gov mirror as a sovereign reference database (the data is public-domain US-government data, mirroring it is unrestricted, sovereignty story holds because we host the mirror).

Replace DRKG with POLARIS's clinical-trial-specific knowledge graph (or substitute the persistent ClinicalTrials.gov mirror).
docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:300:**Why it works:** generator-agnostic (only needs token log-probs which most open-weight inference APIs expose); no retrieval needed; catches both knowledge-fabrication (high entropy) and confabulation (high variance across mirror models); empirically AUC 0.95-0.96.
docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:306:Generate the same answer K times with temperature variation; if all K agree, treat as confident; if variance is high, escalate to LLM-as-judge verifier. Hybrid black-box / white-box approach. Verdict library [^verdict] from Haize Labs operationalises this.
docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:308:**Why it works:** cheap signal (just temperature sampling); catches the long-tail of low-confidence answers without paying judge cost on the bulk of high-confidence cases.

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:712:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:713:12b. **Claim-frame hard constraint (M-38, eliminating under-framed study mentions)**: Rule #12 is asymmetric and STRICT — when you name a specific study, trial, cohort, or experiment by its short name (phase-N trial identifier in clinical; long-run battery cycling test in materials; named longitudinal cohort in epidemiology; named regulatory docket in policy), that sentence — or the IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING sentence in the same paragraph — MUST carry at LEAST THREE frame elements drawn from: sample size / cohort N; baseline value; comparator / control arm; specific dose or intervention level; primary endpoint; timepoint; effect size WITH uncertainty (CI, SD, or p-value). If you cannot produce three of those elements from the cited evidence, DO NOT name the study by its short name — phrase the sentence generically as "one randomized trial showed ... [ev_X]" or "a prospective cohort in the target population reported ... [ev_X]" or "one pooled analysis found ... [ev_X]" or "a long-run cycling test reported ... [ev_X]" instead. This hard floor prevents the failure mode where a sentence names a specific study but gives only a single effect-size number without N, baseline, or comparator — producing a news-style summary mis-labelled with a primary-study name. Concrete templates (use placeholders): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." GOOD (generic when frame is unavailable): "A pre-planned pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials reported [ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — no short-name attribution because pooled data lack per-trial N. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] showed that [INTERVENTION] reduced [ENDPOINT] more than [COMPARATOR] [ev_X]." — names the study with only one frame element (effect direction); rewrite as "A head-to-head trial of [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR] reported greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]" which drops the study name because the frame is too thin. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — names study with only endpoint + effect; rewrite as "One pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]" ONLY if the cited evidence confirms pooled data across two trials. This rule is what converts a LOSE_BOTH on Claim frames into a competitive synthesis.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:714:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.

docs\benchmark\scoring_rubric.md:6:**Scoring philosophy:** **deterministic + measurable**, NOT LLM-as-judge subjective scoring
docs\benchmark\scoring_rubric.md:14:1. **Deterministic** — running the rubric against the same inputs produces the same scores. No reviewer subjectivity, no LLM-as-judge variance.
docs\benchmark\scoring_rubric.md:76:Per-claim citation precision (does the cited source actually support the claim it's attached to?) is qualitative and **cannot be deterministically scored without ground-truth claim-source mappings**. Plan v13 §F names "citation precision/recall ≥ baseline" but for benchmark purposes precision is approximated via a Phase-3 spot-check protocol: human reviewer audits 10 random claim-citation pairs per template, scores `# verified` / 10. The aggregate precision-spot-check is the user-side verification at Phase 3 close. NO LLM-as-judge — would re-introduce the very subjectivity the rubric exists to eliminate.
docs\benchmark\scoring_rubric.md:185:**Total: ~$8–25 USD.** Replaces the eliminated paid evaluator T3 tranche ($8–12k). Massive cost reduction at no loss of validation rigour — because the rubric is deterministic, the expensive part of paid evaluators (trained-judge scoring time) is automated.

 succeeded in 954ms:
  440: 
  441: @dataclass
  442: class LLMCall:
  443:     call_id: str
  444:     role: str
  445:     prompt_messages_present: bool
  446:     request_hash: str | None
  447:     response_metadata: dict   # served {model, provider_name, system_fingerprint, ...}
  448: 
  449: 
  450: def assert_post_run(
  451:     pin: dict,
  452:     control_vars: list[str],
  453:     salt: bytes,
  454:     calls: list[LLMCall],
  455:     retrieval_backends_attempted: set[str],
  456: ) -> dict:
  457:     """Fatal post-run gate (Codex). Any violation ⇒ run INVALID, discard + re-run.
  458: 
  459:     Returns the established per-role served-identity surrogates on success."""
  460:     # config no-drift — rebuild from the SAME resolved surface preflight pinned (not a
  461:     # caller-passed list, which could differ / bypass; Codex iter-2).
  462:     pinned_vars = pin.get("control_vars", control_vars)
  463:     cfg_now = effective_config_hash(build_effective_config(pinned_vars, salt))
  464:     if cfg_now != pin["effective_config_hash"]:
  465:         raise GateError("effective_config drifted between preflight and post-run")
  466:     pins_by_role = {rp["role"]: rp for rp in pin["role_pins"]}
  467:     if not calls:
  468:         raise GateError("no LLM calls captured — completeness check cannot pass")
  469:     # COMPLETENESS: every pinned role must appear (Codex P1 — uncaptured evaluator/judge invisible)
  470:     roles_seen = {c.role for c in calls}
  471:     missing_roles = set(pins_by_role) - roles_seen
  472:     if missing_roles:
  473:         raise GateError(f"completeness: pinned role(s) with no captured LLM call: {missing_roles}")
  474:     surrogate_by_role: dict[str, set[str]] = {}
  475:     for c in calls:
  476:         if not (c.prompt_messages_present and c.request_hash and c.response_metadata):
  477:             raise GateError(f"call {c.call_id}: incomplete capture (prompt/request_hash/metadata)")
  478:         rp = pins_by_role.get(c.role)
  479:         if rp is None:
  480:             raise GateError(f"call {c.call_id}: role {c.role!r} not pinned")
  481:         for fld in rp["surrogate_fields"]:
  482:             if fld not in c.response_metadata:
  483:                 raise GateError(f"call {c.call_id}: served metadata missing surrogate field {fld!r}")
  484:         # EXACT provider + EXACT full-slug model match (Codex P1 — no loose substring).
  485:         # I-bug-944 (#925 smoke #13): provider comparison is case-insensitive (OpenRouter
  486:         # returns "Fireworks" / "DeepInfra" with title case while the pin env var
  487:         # OPENROUTER_PROVIDER_ORDER is documented lower-case; case-mismatch is identity-
  488:         # equivalent and must not gate-fail an otherwise full-power run). Model slug stays
  489:         # case-sensitive — slugs are canonical.
  490:         served_provider = (c.response_metadata.get("provider_name") or "").strip().lower()
  491:         pinned_provider = (rp["provider_name"] or "").strip().lower()
  492:         if served_provider != pinned_provider:
  493:             raise GateError(f"call {c.call_id}: served provider {c.response_metadata.get('provider_name')!r} != pinned {rp['provider_name']!r}")
  494:         # I-bug-945 (#931): accept served model matching EITHER the pinned alias OR the
  495:         # canonical_slug resolved at preflight. The OpenRouter chat-completions response
  496:         # returns `model=<canonical_slug>` while the env pin is the alias; both are identity-
  497:         # equivalent and recorded in the persisted pin (pathB_gate_pin.json).
  498:         served_model = c.response_metadata.get("model")
  499:         accepted_models = {rp["model_slug"]}
  500:         if rp.get("canonical_slug"):
  501:             accepted_models.add(rp["canonical_slug"])
  502:         if served_model not in accepted_models:
  503:             raise GateError(
  504:                 f"call {c.call_id}: served model {served_model!r} matches neither pinned "
  505:                 f"alias {rp['model_slug']!r} nor canonical_slug {rp.get('canonical_slug')!r}"
  506:             )
  507:         # I-bug-945 P2#4 (Codex): normalize served `model` to the alias before surrogate
  508:         # compute, so a same-role mix of alias and canonical_slug calls produces a single
  509:         # surrogate value (otherwise raw-model drift would false-fail the mid-run check).
  510:         normalized_metadata = dict(c.response_metadata)
  511:         normalized_metadata["model"] = rp["model_slug"]
  512:         surrogate_by_role.setdefault(c.role, set()).add(_role_surrogate(normalized_metadata, rp["surrogate_fields"]))
  513:     # per-role served identity must be SINGLE-VALUED across the run (no mid-run drift, Codex P1)
  514:     for role, ids in surrogate_by_role.items():
  515:         if len(ids) != 1:
  516:             raise GateError(f"role {role}: served-identity surrogate drifted across calls ({len(ids)} distinct)")
  517:     # required retrieval backends were ACTUALLY attempted (Codex iter-5 P2)
  518:     required = set(_REQUIRED_RETRIEVAL_CREDS_TO_BACKENDS.values())
  519:     not_attempted = required - retrieval_backends_attempted
  520:     if not_attempted:
  521:         raise GateError(f"required retrieval backends never attempted this run: {not_attempted}")
  522:     return {"served_identity_by_role": {r: next(iter(ids)) for r, ids in surrogate_by_role.items()}}
  523:

  526:     "SERPER_API_KEY": "serper",
  527:     "SEMANTIC_SCHOLAR_API_KEY": "semantic_scholar",
  528: }

  143: ) -> FourRoleEvaluationResult:
  144:     """Drive the per-claim 4-role pipeline, apply the SINGLE binding D8 gate, persist the KG.
  145: 
  146:     Pure orchestration over the INJECTED `transport` (no network, no spend). For EACH claim:
  147:     run `run_claim_pipeline`, collect its `D8ClaimRow` + served-identity records + final
  148:     verdict, and — only on a VERIFIED final verdict — credit that claim's canonical
  149:     `covered_element_ids` into the ledger. Then run `apply_d8_release_policy` ONCE over the
  150:     collected rows (D8 is the headline gate) and write every per-claim outcome to the snowball
  151:     `VerifiedClaimGraphStore` under `run_dir`.
  152: 
  153:     Fail-closed guards (Codex P2): raises `ValueError` on an empty claim set, an empty
  154:     canonical required-element denominator, a blank/duplicate `claim_id`, or a missing role
  155:     slug — never a vacuous pass and never a synthesized id.
  156:     """
  157:     # (P2) NO vacuous pass: an empty claim set or an empty canonical coverage denominator must
  158:     # fail LOUD here, before any D8 call — fraction()==1.0 over an empty required set would
  159:     # otherwise release "nothing" as all-clear.
  160:     if not claims:
  161:         raise ValueError(
  162:             "run_four_role_evaluation: no claims supplied; a 4-role evaluation over zero "
  163:             "claims cannot produce a release decision (fail-closed, no vacuous pass)."
  164:         )
  165:     if not coverage_ledger.required_element_ids:
  166:         raise ValueError(
  167:             "run_four_role_evaluation: coverage_ledger.required_element_ids is empty; the "
  168:             "coverage denominator MUST be the canonical per-question required-element set "
  169:             "(fail-closed, no vacuous pass over an empty denominator)."
  170:         )
  171:     # (Codex sub-PR-6 diff P1, LETHAL safety invariant) The coverage NUMERATOR must be rebuilt
  172:     # here SOLELY from VERIFIED final verdicts — never trusted from the caller. A prefilled
  173:     # `covered_element_ids` would let a Sentinel-UNGROUNDED claim that we correctly downgrade to
  174:     # UNSUPPORTED still ride pre-credited coverage and release. Reject a non-empty incoming set
  175:     # (fail LOUD), then credit a FRESH internal ledger only on VERIFIED finals below.
  176:     if coverage_ledger.covered_element_ids:
  177:         raise ValueError(
  178:             "run_four_role_evaluation: coverage_ledger.covered_element_ids must be EMPTY on "
  179:             "input; the coverage numerator is rebuilt here from VERIFIED final verdicts only, so "
  180:             "a prefilled numerator cannot let an ungrounded/downgraded claim ride pre-credited "
  181:             "coverage (fail-closed)."
  182:         )
  183:     internal_ledger = CoverageLedger(
  184:         required_element_ids=list(coverage_ledger.required_element_ids),
  185:         covered_element_ids=set(),
  186:     )
  187:     missing_slugs = [key for key in _REQUIRED_ROLE_SLUG_KEYS if not model_slugs.get(key)]
  188:     if missing_slugs:
  189:         raise ValueError(
  190:             f"run_four_role_evaluation: model_slugs missing required role slug(s) "
  191:             f"{missing_slugs}; the pipeline needs mirror/sentinel/judge pins."
  192:         )
  193: 
  194:     # (P2) NO synthesized ids: every claim must carry a non-blank, unique existing claim_id.
  195:     seen_ids: set[str] = set()
  196:     for claim in claims:
  197:         claim_id = (claim.claim_id or "").strip()
  198:         if not claim_id:
  199:             raise ValueError(
  200:                 "run_four_role_evaluation: a claim has a blank claim_id; claim_ids are "
  201:                 "caller-supplied (verified-sentence / section ids) and never synthesized."
  202:             )
  203:         if claim_id in seen_ids:
  204:             raise ValueError(
  205:                 f"run_four_role_evaluation: duplicate claim_id {claim_id!r}; ids must be "
  206:                 f"unique so rewrite/gap traceability does not collide."
  207:             )
  208:         seen_ids.add(claim_id)
  209: 
  210:     d8_rows: list[D8ClaimRow] = []
  211:     all_records: list[RoleCallRecord] = []

  214:     kg_store = VerifiedClaimGraphStore(run_dir=run_dir)
  215:     try:
  216:         for claim in claims:
  217:             result = run_claim_pipeline(
  218:                 transport,
  219:                 claim_id=claim.claim_id,
  220:                 claim=claim.claim_text,
  221:                 evidence_documents=claim.evidence_documents,

  240:             kg_store.write_claim(

  242:                 claim_id=claim.claim_id,
  243:                 verdict=result.final_verdict,
  244:                 role_verdicts={

  252:                         if result.sentinel_result is not None
  253:                         else None
  254:                     ),
  255:                     "raw_judge_verdict": result.raw_judge_verdict,

  272:         rewrite_already_attempted=rewrite_already_attempted,

   66: 
   67: class RecordingTransport:
   68:     """Wrap an injected `RoleTransport`; record EVERY completion before returning it.
   69: 
   70:     On each `complete(request)` the wrapper appends a `RoleCallRecord(role, model_slug,
   71:     served_model, raw_text, parsed=None)` to `self.records` BEFORE returning the underlying
   72:     response (Codex iter-2 P1-4). Because the record is appended before the adapter sees the
   73:     response — and therefore before the adapter can parse or raise — the served-identity
   74:     record survives even on the fail-closed paths (a Mirror pass-1 that then raises
   75:     `MirrorCitationError`). `parsed` is left None here: it is the role contract that parses,
   76:     and the parsed sub-results are carried separately on `ClaimPipelineResult`.
   77:     """
   78: 
   79:     def __init__(self, transport: RoleTransport) -> None:
   80:         self._transport = transport
   81:         self.records: list[RoleCallRecord] = []
   82: 
   83:     def complete(self, request: RoleRequest) -> RoleResponse:
   84:         response = self._transport.complete(request)
   85:         # Append BEFORE returning so a downstream adapter raise cannot drop the record.
   86:         self.records.append(
   87:             RoleCallRecord(
   88:                 role=request.role,
   89:                 model_slug=request.model_slug,
   90:                 served_model=response.served_model,
   91:                 raw_text=response.raw_text,
   92:                 parsed=None,
   93:             )
   94:         )
   95:         return response
   96: 
   97: 
   98: @dataclass
   99: class ClaimPipelineResult:
  100:     """The full per-claim orchestration result.
  101: 
  102:     `d8_row` carries the POST-OVERRIDE `final_verdict` in `D8ClaimRow.verdict`.
  103:     `raw_judge_verdict` preserves the Judge's pre-override verdict (None if the Judge never
  104:     ran because Mirror failed closed). `records` is the complete served-identity audit trail
  105:     from the `RecordingTransport` (complete even on fail-closed paths). The raw
  106:     `mirror_result` / `sentinel_result` / `judge_result` are preserved for auditability and
  107:     are None where that stage failed closed / did not run.
  108:     """
  109: 
  110:     d8_row: D8ClaimRow
  111:     raw_judge_verdict: Verdict | None
  112:     final_verdict: Verdict
  113:     records: list[RoleCallRecord]
  114:     mirror_result: MirrorPass2 | None
  115:     sentinel_result: SentinelResult | None
  116:     judge_result: Verdict | None
  117: 
  118: 
  119: def _first_grounded_citation_id(mirror_records: list[RoleCallRecord]) -> str | None:
  120:     """Extract a grounded citation doc_id from the Mirror pass-1 record, else None.
  121: 
  122:     The grounded doc_ids live on the pass-1 `MirrorPass1.citation_spans` (the pass-2
  123:     `MirrorPass2` carries only a classification + hash, NOT doc_ids). `run_mirror` returns
  124:     its OWN record list whose pass-1 record's `parsed` is a `MirrorPass1`; the first grounded
  125:     span's first doc_id is used for D8 gap reporting. Returns None if no grounded span exists.
  126:     """
  127:     for record in mirror_records:
  128:         parsed = record.parsed
  129:         if isinstance(parsed, MirrorPass1) and parsed.citation_spans:
  130:             for span in parsed.citation_spans:
  131:                 if span.doc_ids:
  132:                     return span.doc_ids[0]
  133:     return None
  134: 
  135: 
  136: def _compose_final_verdict(
  137:     *,
  138:     mirror_failed_closed: bool,
  139:     sentinel_result: SentinelResult | None,
  140:     raw_judge_verdict: Verdict | None,
  141: ) -> Verdict:
  142:     """LOCKED fail-closed composition rule (Codex iter-2 P1-1).
  143: 
  144:     A hallucination can NEVER reach VERIFIED; a worse Judge verdict is NEVER upgraded.
  145: 
  146:       (1) Mirror raised MirrorCitationError/MirrorBindingError (no grounded/bound citation)
  147:           -> UNSUPPORTED, regardless of Judge. A claim with no grounded citation can never be
  148:           VERIFIED. (On this path the Judge never ran, so raw_judge_verdict is None.)
  149:       (2) ELSE if Sentinel == UNGROUNDED OR Sentinel.parsed_ok is False
  150:           -> if raw Judge verdict is VERIFIED/PARTIAL, OVERRIDE to UNSUPPORTED;
  151:              if raw Judge verdict is FABRICATED/UNREACHABLE/UNSUPPORTED, PRESERVE it
  152:              (never upgrade a worse verdict to merely UNSUPPORTED).
  153:       (3) ELSE -> raw_judge_verdict (Sentinel grounded + parsed_ok; trust the arbiter).
  154:     """
  155:     # (1) Mirror fail-closed -> UNSUPPORTED.
  156:     if mirror_failed_closed:
  157:         return _VERDICT_UNSUPPORTED
  158: 
  159:     # raw_judge_verdict is non-None here: the Judge ran (Mirror succeeded). It fails LOUD on a
  160:     # non-enum token (JudgeEnumError propagates from run_judge), so it is a valid Verdict.
  161:     assert raw_judge_verdict is not None  # invariant: Judge ran iff Mirror succeeded.
  162: 
  163:     # (2) Sentinel UNGROUNDED or unparsed -> downgrade an apparently-good Judge verdict.
  164:     sentinel_unsafe = sentinel_result is None or (
  165:         sentinel_result.verdict == SentinelVerdict.UNGROUNDED
  166:         or not sentinel_result.parsed_ok
  167:     )
  168:     if sentinel_unsafe:
  169:         if raw_judge_verdict in _SENTINEL_OVERRIDE_DOWNGRADE_FROM:
  170:             return _VERDICT_UNSUPPORTED
  171:         return raw_judge_verdict  # FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE / UNSUPPORTED preserved.
  172: 
  173:     # (3) Sentinel grounded + parsed_ok -> the Judge's verdict stands.
  174:     return raw_judge_verdict
  175: 
  176: 
  177: def run_claim_pipeline(
  178:     transport: RoleTransport,
  179:     *,
  180:     claim_id: str,
  181:     claim: str,
  182:     evidence_documents: list[EvidenceDocument],
  183:     severity: str,
  184:     s0_categories: list[str],
  185:     model_slugs: dict[str, str],
  186:     timestamp: str,
  187: ) -> ClaimPipelineResult:
  188:     """Run Mirror -> Sentinel -> Judge over the injected transport for ONE claim.
  189: 
  190:     `model_slugs` maps role -> pinned slug (keys: "mirror", "sentinel", "judge"). `claim_id`
  191:     is REQUIRED and flows verbatim into `D8ClaimRow.claim_id` (never synthesized). `timestamp`
  192:     is passed through for the caller's audit record (this function does NOT call
  193:     datetime.now()).
  194: 
  195:     Composition is FAIL-CLOSED per `_compose_final_verdict`. On a Mirror fail-closed
  196:     (MirrorCitationError/MirrorBindingError) the pipeline SHORT-CIRCUITS: Sentinel and Judge
  197:     do not run, `final_verdict = UNSUPPORTED`, and the raw sub-results are None — but the
  198:     RecordingTransport still holds the served-identity record for the Mirror call(s) that did
  199:     fire, so the identity gate sees them.
  200:     """
  201:     recording = RecordingTransport(transport)
  202: 
  203:     mirror_slug = model_slugs["mirror"]
  204:     sentinel_slug = model_slugs["sentinel"]
  205:     judge_slug = model_slugs["judge"]
  206: 
  207:     mirror_result: MirrorPass2 | None = None
  208:     sentinel_result: SentinelResult | None = None
  209:     judge_result: Verdict | None = None
  210:     raw_judge_verdict: Verdict | None = None
  211:     citation_id: str | None = None
  212:     mirror_failed_closed = False
  213: 
  214:     # --- stage 14: Mirror (fail CLOSED) ----------------------------------------------
  215:     # Catch the two grounding/binding errors EXPLICITLY (NOT `except: pass`) so they drive the
  216:     # UNSUPPORTED override; any OTHER exception propagates (a transport fault is not a verdict).
  217:     try:
  218:         mirror_result, mirror_records = run_mirror(
  219:             recording, claim, evidence_documents, model_slug=mirror_slug
  220:         )
  221:         citation_id = _first_grounded_citation_id(mirror_records)
  222:     except (MirrorCitationError, MirrorBindingError):
  223:         mirror_failed_closed = True
  224: 
  225:     # --- stage 15 + 16: Sentinel -> Judge (only if Mirror produced a grounded claim) -----
  226:     if not mirror_failed_closed:
  227:         sentinel_result, _sentinel_records = run_sentinel(
  228:             recording, claim, evidence_documents, model_slug=sentinel_slug
  229:         )
  230:         evidence_text = "\n\n".join(doc.text for doc in evidence_documents)
  231:         # Judge fails LOUD by design: a non-enum token raises JudgeEnumError, which we do NOT
  232:         # catch — a missing/garbage arbiter verdict must propagate, never coerce to a default.
  233:         raw_judge_verdict, _judge_records = run_judge(
  234:             recording,
  235:             claim,
  236:             evidence_text,
  237:             mirror_verdict=str(mirror_result.classification),
  238:             sentinel_verdict=sentinel_result.verdict.value,
  239:             model_slug=judge_slug,
  240:         )
  241:         judge_result = raw_judge_verdict
  242: 
  243:     final_verdict = _compose_final_verdict(
  244:         mirror_failed_closed=mirror_failed_closed,
  245:         sentinel_result=sentinel_result,
  246:         raw_judge_verdict=raw_judge_verdict,
  247:     )
  248: 
  249:     d8_row = D8ClaimRow(
  250:         claim_id=claim_id,
  251:         severity=severity,
  252:         verdict=final_verdict,
  253:         citation_id=citation_id,
  254:         s0_categories=list(s0_categories),
  255:     )
  256: 
  257:     return ClaimPipelineResult(
  258:         d8_row=d8_row,
  259:         raw_judge_verdict=raw_judge_verdict,
  260:         final_verdict=final_verdict,
  261:         records=recording.records,
  262:         mirror_result=mirror_result,
  263:         sentinel_result=sentinel_result,
  264:         judge_result=judge_result,
  265:     )

 succeeded in 939ms:
    1: """Mirror (Cohere Command-A+) two-pass RAG/JSON contract.
    2: 
    3: Cohere `response_format` (JSON mode) is NOT supported together with `documents`/`tools`
    4: (F2, confirmed in I-meta-002 iter-2 verdict). So the Mirror role is TWO-PASS:
    5:   pass-1: RAG-with-citations  -> grounded answer text + citation spans (each span its doc_id)
    6:   pass-2: JSON classification -> bound to pass-1 by a content_hash
    7: 
    8: The pass-2 classification MUST be of the SAME artifact pass-1 produced, not a regenerated
    9: or normalized one. (iter-2 fix, Codex P1-a): the binding hash covers BOTH the answer text
   10: AND the ordered citation bindings `(span_start, span_end, doc_id)` — NOT the answer text
   11: alone — so identical answer text with swapped or missing citation bindings does NOT pass
   12: the hash check.
   13: 
   14: Citation span format: self-host Cohere emits `<co>...</co:doc_ids>` spans (doc_ids is a
   15: comma-separated list). `parse_cohere_citations` parses that form and tolerates an empty
   16: input. There is no live Cohere in this PR; the `<co>` fixture IS the assumed self-host
   17: span shape, documented here rather than implied as verified output.
   18: """
   19: 
   20: from __future__ import annotations
   21: 
   22: import hashlib
   23: import json
   24: import re
   25: from dataclasses import dataclass, field
   26: 
   27: 
   28: @dataclass(frozen=True)
   29: class CitationSpan:
   30:     """One grounded citation span: a [span_start, span_end) char range over the answer
   31:     text, attached to one or more source doc_ids."""
   32: 
   33:     span_start: int
   34:     span_end: int
   35:     doc_ids: tuple[str, ...]
   36: 
   37: 
   38: @dataclass
   39: class MirrorPass1:
   40:     """Pass-1 output: the grounded answer text plus its citation spans."""
   41: 
   42:     answer_text: str
   43:     citation_spans: list[CitationSpan] = field(default_factory=list)
   44: 
   45: 
   46: @dataclass
   47: class MirrorPass2:
   48:     """Pass-2 output: the JSON classification, bound to pass-1 by `content_hash`."""
   49: 
   50:     content_hash: str
   51:     classification: str
   52:     rationale: str | None = None
   53: 
   54: 
   55: # Field key for the embedded binding hash in the pass-2 input dict.
   56: _CONTENT_HASH_KEY = "content_hash"
   57: _ANSWER_TEXT_KEY = "answer_text"
   58: 
   59: # Self-host Cohere span: `<co>covered text</co:doc_a,doc_b>`. The doc_ids list is
   60: # captured from the closing tag. Whitespace-tolerant around the doc_ids.
   61: _CO_SPAN_RE = re.compile(r"<co>(.*?)</co:\s*([^>]*?)\s*>", re.DOTALL)
   62: 
   63: 
   64: def _canonical_binding(pass1: MirrorPass1) -> str:
   65:     """Deterministic canonical serialization of the pass-1 artifact for hashing.
   66: 
   67:     Covers the answer text AND the ordered list of `(span_start, span_end, doc_id)` tuples.
   68:     Multi-doc spans are expanded to one tuple per doc_id, and the full tuple list is sorted,
   69:     so the serialization is independent of span/doc_id authoring order but still sensitive
   70:     to ANY change in the (start, end, doc_id) bindings. The exact same serializer is used
   71:     by both `build_pass2_input` and `verify_pass2_binding`.
   72: 
   73:     INJECTIVITY: the answer text and the binding list are wrapped as the two elements of a
   74:     single JSON array. Because the answer is JSON-string-escaped, there is NO ambiguous
   75:     delimiter byte a crafted doc_id (which may legitimately contain spaces or brackets) could
   76:     inject to collide two distinct (answer, bindings) pairs onto the same serialization —
   77:     unlike a flat `answer + " " + bindings` concatenation. Resolves brief question 2 (P1-a).
   78:     """
   79:     binding_tuples: list[tuple[int, int, str]] = []
   80:     for span in pass1.citation_spans:
   81:         for doc_id in span.doc_ids:
   82:             binding_tuples.append((span.span_start, span.span_end, doc_id))
   83:     binding_tuples.sort()
   84:     return json.dumps([pass1.answer_text, binding_tuples], separators=(",", ":"))
   85: 
   86: 
   87: def _compute_content_hash(pass1: MirrorPass1) -> str:
   88:     """sha256 over the canonical (answer_text + citation bindings) serialization."""
   89:     canonical = _canonical_binding(pass1)
   90:     return hashlib.sha256(canonical.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
   91: 
   92: 
   93: def build_pass2_input(pass1: MirrorPass1) -> dict:
   94:     """Build the input dict handed to pass-2, embedding the composite `content_hash`.
   95: 
   96:     The hash is computed over BOTH the answer text and the ordered citation bindings
   97:     (P1-a), so pass-2 can only validly classify the exact (answer + citations) artifact
   98:     pass-1 produced.
   99:     """
  100:     return {
  101:         _ANSWER_TEXT_KEY: pass1.answer_text,
  102:         _CONTENT_HASH_KEY: _compute_content_hash(pass1),
  103:     }
  104: 
  105: 
  106: def verify_pass2_binding(pass1: MirrorPass1, pass2: MirrorPass2) -> bool:
  107:     """True iff pass-2 classified the SAME (answer + citations) artifact as pass-1.
  108: 
  109:     Recomputes the composite hash from pass-1 and compares it to `pass2.content_hash`.
  110:     Returns False if the answer text was regenerated/normalized OR if any citation binding
  111:     (span_start, span_end, doc_id) was swapped or dropped — even when the answer text is
  112:     byte-identical.
  113:     """
  114:     return _compute_content_hash(pass1) == pass2.content_hash
  115: 
  116: 
  117: def parse_cohere_citations(raw: str) -> list[CitationSpan]:
  118:     """Parse self-host Cohere `<co>...</co:doc_ids>` spans into CitationSpans.
  119: 
  120:     `span_start`/`span_end` are the [start, end) char offsets of the covered text WITHIN
  121:     the cleaned answer (tags stripped), reconstructed as the spans are consumed left to
  122:     right. `doc_ids` is the comma-separated list from the closing tag (empty entries
  123:     dropped). Tolerates empty input (returns []) and tolerates a span with no doc_ids.
  124: 
  125:     Managed-form tolerance: a managed Cohere `message.citations` offset payload contains no
  126:     `<co>` spans, so this parser returns [] for it BY DESIGN (it does not crash). Full
  127:     managed-offset parsing is sub-PR-4's adapter; this contract covers the self-host span
  128:     form only.
  129:     """
  130:     if not raw:
  131:         return []
  132: 
  133:     spans: list[CitationSpan] = []
  134:     cleaned_len = 0  # running length of the answer text with tags removed
  135:     cursor = 0       # position in raw
  136:     for match in _CO_SPAN_RE.finditer(raw):
  137:         # Plain text before this span contributes to the cleaned-text offset.
  138:         cleaned_len += len(raw[cursor:match.start()])
  139:         covered_text = match.group(1)
  140:         doc_ids_raw = match.group(2)
  141:         doc_ids = tuple(d.strip() for d in doc_ids_raw.split(",") if d.strip())
  142:         span_start = cleaned_len
  143:         span_end = span_start + len(covered_text)
  144:         spans.append(CitationSpan(span_start=span_start, span_end=span_end, doc_ids=doc_ids))
  145:         cleaned_len = span_end
  146:         cursor = match.end()
  147:     return spans

    1: """Judge (Qwen3.6) verdict contract — hard-enum, NO silent default.
    2: 
    3: Reuses the canonical 5-enum verdict shape from `claim_audit_scorer.Verdict`
    4: (VERIFIED / PARTIAL / UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE). It is IMPORTED, never
    5: redefined, so there is exactly one verdict vocabulary in the codebase.
    6: 
    7: The Judge runs self-hosted under vLLM with a hard enum constraint
    8: (`structured_outputs.choice`, the correct spelling — `guided_choice` is deprecated, F4).
    9: `JUDGE_CHOICES` exposes the exact allowed token list for that constraint (PR4).
   10: 
   11: This module also holds the `source_missing` split classifier (`classify_unreachable`),
   12: which separates a genuine artifact/fetch miss (UNREACHABLE) from a fabricated citation
   13: identity (FABRICATED). The wiring into the release gate is sub-PR-3.
   14: """
   15: 
   16: from __future__ import annotations
   17: 
   18: from typing import Iterable, get_args
   19: 
   20: from src.polaris_graph.benchmark.claim_audit_scorer import Verdict
   21: 
   22: # The exact allowed verdict tokens, derived from the canonical Literal so the two can
   23: # never drift. Used by PR4 for the vLLM `structured_outputs.choice` constraint.
   24: JUDGE_CHOICES: list[str] = list(get_args(Verdict))
   25: 
   26: # Fetch-miss subtypes: a real artifact/fetch failure for an IN-POOL source -> UNREACHABLE.
   27: _FETCH_MISS_SUBTYPES = ("paywall", "robots", "fetch_failure")
   28: 
   29: # Classification outputs of classify_unreachable.
   30: _CLASS_UNREACHABLE = "UNREACHABLE"
   31: _CLASS_FABRICATED = "FABRICATED"
   32: 
   33: 
   34: class JudgeEnumError(ValueError):
   35:     """Raised when a raw Judge output is not exactly one of the 5 canonical verdicts.
   36: 
   37:     There is NO silent default. A non-enum token is a hard failure (clinical safety):
   38:     the caller must treat it as a parse error and escalate, never coerce it to a verdict.
   39:     """
   40: 
   41: 
   42: def parse_judge_verdict(raw: str) -> Verdict:
   43:     """Parse a raw Judge output into the canonical 5-enum `Verdict`.
   44: 
   45:     The match is exact against `JUDGE_CHOICES` after stripping surrounding whitespace.
   46:     Any non-enum token — garbage, empty, lowercase-unknown, partial — raises
   47:     `JudgeEnumError`. There is deliberately NO case-folding and NO fuzzy match: the Judge
   48:     is enum-constrained at decode time (vLLM), so anything off-enum signals a real fault.
   49:     """
   50:     if not isinstance(raw, str):
   51:         raise JudgeEnumError(f"Judge output is not a string: {type(raw)!r}")
   52:     token = raw.strip()
   53:     if token not in JUDGE_CHOICES:
   54:         raise JudgeEnumError(
   55:             f"Judge output {token!r} is not one of the {len(JUDGE_CHOICES)} canonical "
   56:             f"verdicts {JUDGE_CHOICES}"
   57:         )
   58:     # token is now a member of the Verdict Literal domain.
   59:     return token  # type: ignore[return-value]
   60: 
   61: 
   62: def classify_unreachable(
   63:     subtype: str | None,
   64:     citation_id: str | None,
   65:     evidence_pool_ids: Iterable[str],
   66: ) -> str:
   67:     """Split a 'source could not be confirmed' case into UNREACHABLE vs FABRICATED.
   68: 
   69:     LOCKED PRECEDENCE (I-meta-002 iter-2 P1-b) — fabricated identity wins FIRST:
   70:       (1) if `citation_id` is None/empty OR `citation_id` is NOT in `evidence_pool_ids`
   71:           -> FABRICATED, regardless of `subtype`. A fabricated/unknown citation identity
   72:           must NOT be laundered as a fetch failure.
   73:       (2) ELSE if `subtype` in {paywall, robots, fetch_failure} -> UNREACHABLE.
   74: 
   75:     `evidence_pool_ids` contract: it is the set of CANONICAL PRE-FETCH evidence IDs — every
   76:     source the pipeline selected/attempted, INCLUDING records whose fetch later FAILED
   77:     (paywall/robots/fetch_failure). A genuine fetch failure therefore still has its
   78:     `citation_id` present in the pool -> correctly UNREACHABLE; only an id that was never a
   79:     selected source -> FABRICATED.
   80: 
   81:     Anything else (an in-pool id whose subtype is not a known fetch-miss, e.g.
   82:     `source_missing`/None/unknown) is OUT of this contract's domain and is a programming
   83:     error, so it raises rather than silently defaulting (LAW II fail-loud).
   84:     """
   85:     pool = set(evidence_pool_ids)
   86:     # (1) fabricated identity check — evaluated BEFORE the subtype branch.
   87:     if not citation_id or citation_id not in pool:
   88:         return _CLASS_FABRICATED
   89:     # (2) in-pool id: a real fetch miss is UNREACHABLE.
   90:     if subtype in _FETCH_MISS_SUBTYPES:
   91:         return _CLASS_UNREACHABLE
   92:     raise ValueError(
   93:         f"classify_unreachable: in-pool citation {citation_id!r} with subtype {subtype!r} "
   94:         f"is outside the fetch-miss contract domain {_FETCH_MISS_SUBTYPES}"
   95:     )

    1: """Sentinel (IBM Granite Guardian 4.1) groundedness contract — FAIL CLOSED.
    2: 
    3: Granite Guardian groundedness polarity (primary source: ibm.com/granite/docs/models/guardian,
    4: confirmed in I-meta-002 iter-2 verdict F3):
    5:     output is `<score>yes|no</score>` (NOT JSON), where
    6:       yes = risk present       -> the answer is UNGROUNDED
    7:       no  = risk not present    -> the answer is GROUNDED
    8: 
    9: This is the LETHAL inversion guard. The two failure modes that hurt patients are:
   10:   (1) silently reading `yes` as GROUNDED (polarity inversion), and
   11:   (2) silently defaulting an unparseable/missing/ambiguous output to GROUNDED.
   12: Both are prevented here: the polarity is hard-coded yes->UNGROUNDED, and EVERY
   13: non-clean parse falls to the safe side (UNGROUNDED) with parsed_ok=False so the
   14: caller can escalate. There is NO code path that returns GROUNDED on bad input.
   15: 
   16: Contrast with `entailment_judge.py`, which fails OPEN on transient error; Sentinel
   17: deliberately fails CLOSED, so it is a SEPARATE contract, not a reuse.
   18: """
   19:

   21: 
   22: import re
   23: from enum import Enum
   24: from typing import NamedTuple
   25: 
   26: 
   27: class SentinelVerdict(Enum):
   28:     """Groundedness verdict for one Sentinel score."""
   29: 
   30:     GROUNDED = "grounded"
   31:     UNGROUNDED = "ungrounded"
   32: 
   33: 
   34: class SentinelResult(NamedTuple):
   35:     """Result of parsing one Sentinel `<score>` output.
   36: 
   37:     Returned on EVERY path. `parsed_ok` is True only on a clean, unambiguous parse;
   38:     on any malformed/missing/ambiguous input it is False and `verdict` is forced to the
   39:     safe (UNGROUNDED) side so the caller can escalate rather than trust a bad score.
   40:     """
   41: 
   42:     verdict: SentinelVerdict
   43:     parsed_ok: bool
   44: 
   45: 
   46: # The canonical Granite Guardian score tokens (LOCKED polarity, F3).
   47: _SCORE_TOKEN_YES = "yes"
   48: _SCORE_TOKEN_NO = "no"
   49: 
   50: # Map the canonical score token to its groundedness verdict. yes=risk=UNGROUNDED.
   51: _SCORE_TOKEN_TO_VERDICT = {
   52:     _SCORE_TOKEN_YES: SentinelVerdict.UNGROUNDED,
   53:     _SCORE_TOKEN_NO: SentinelVerdict.GROUNDED,
   54: }
   55: 
   56: # STRICT ENVELOPE: the WHOLE output must be exactly one `<score>yes|no</score>` element,
   57: # with only surrounding whitespace allowed (and inner whitespace around the token). We
   58: # `fullmatch` the entire raw string, so ANY surrounding prose, a second (even malformed)
   59: # score tag, stray markup, or an off-enum body fails the match and falls to the safe side.
   60: # This single anchored rule subsumes the weaker "count the matches/tags" guards (which let
   61: # `<score>no</score><score>maybe` and `prefix <score>no</score> suffix` slip through as a
   62: # silent GROUNDED — Codex sub-PR-2 diff P0 iter-1/iter-2 + P1 iter-3). The token group is
   63: # constrained to yes|no so a clean match can never carry an off-enum body.
   64: #
   65: # NOTE for PR4 (adapter): if the SERVED Granite Guardian build emits an additional token
   66: # (e.g. a trailing `<confidence>...` line) alongside the score, this contract must be
   67: # EXTENDED with that exact verified format — never loosened to "tag present anywhere".
   68: # `re.ASCII` is REQUIRED alongside IGNORECASE: without it, Unicode case-folding accepts
   69: # homoglyphs like U+017F LONG S ('ſ') as 's', so `<ſcore>no</ſcore>` would match and return
   70: # a silent GROUNDED (Codex sub-PR-2 diff P1 iter-4). ASCII mode folds only a-z/A-Z and limits
   71: # `\s` to ASCII whitespace, so the envelope must be the verified ASCII `<score>yes|no</score>`.
   72: _STRICT_SCORE_RE = re.compile(
   73:     r"\s*<score>\s*(yes|no)\s*</score>\s*", re.IGNORECASE | re.ASCII
   74: )
   75: 
   76: 
   77: def parse_sentinel_score(raw: str) -> SentinelResult:
   78:     """Parse a raw Granite Guardian groundedness output into a SentinelResult.
   79: 
   80:     Mapping (LOCKED, F3): `<score>yes</score>` -> UNGROUNDED, `<score>no</score>` -> GROUNDED.
   81:     Case- and whitespace-tolerant.
   82: 
   83:     FAIL CLOSED: any output that is not EXACTLY one `<score>yes|no</score>` element
   84:     (surrounding whitespace aside) -> UNGROUNDED with parsed_ok=False. NEVER returns
   85:     GROUNDED on bad input. Surrounding prose, a second/partial score tag, off-enum body,
   86:     missing tag, or non-string are ALL treated as failed parses, not best-effort guesses.
   87:     parsed_ok=True is reserved for a single clean score envelope.
   88:     """
   89:     if not isinstance(raw, str):
   90:         return SentinelResult(SentinelVerdict.UNGROUNDED, parsed_ok=False)
   91: 
   92:     # Anchor on the WHOLE output. fullmatch fails on any prefix/suffix/extra/partial markup,
   93:     # so the only parsed_ok=True paths are a lone `<score>yes</score>` or `<score>no</score>`.
   94:     match = _STRICT_SCORE_RE.fullmatch(raw)
   95:     if match is None:
   96:         return SentinelResult(SentinelVerdict.UNGROUNDED, parsed_ok=False)
   97: 
   98:     token = match.group(1).lower()
   99:     verdict = _SCORE_TOKEN_TO_VERDICT.get(token)
  100:     if verdict is None:
  101:         # Defensive: the regex constrains the group to yes|no, so this is unreachable;
  102:         # keep the fail-closed branch so a future regex change cannot leak GROUNDED.
  103:         return SentinelResult(SentinelVerdict.UNGROUNDED, parsed_ok=False)
  104: 
  105:     return SentinelResult(verdict, parsed_ok=True)

 succeeded in 875ms:
    1: """I-meta-001 (#933) — Architecture lock verifier + propagation manifest.
    2: 
    3: This module is the runtime gate that asserts the running codebase honors the
    4: machine-readable architecture lock at ``config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml``.
    5: 
    6: Two surfaces:
    7: 
    8: 1. ``verify_lock_against_code()`` — preflight assertion. Loads the lock YAML,
    9:    compares declared model_slug/family/env_var triples against the actual code
   10:    defaults + family registry + env-var presence. Raises ``LockMismatch`` if
   11:    any role's declared truth differs from runtime truth.
   12: 
   13: 2. ``check_propagation_manifest()`` — promotes ``status: codex_approved_pending_operator_signature``
   14:    to ``locked`` once ALL checkpoints are true:
   15:      - this file committed (tracked by git)
   16:      - source_doc committed
   17:      - canonical_pin.txt includes this file's SHA
   18:      - code_defaults_match (calls verify_lock_against_code)
   19:      - tests_pass (called explicitly by CI; advisory in this module)
   20: 
   21: The lock cannot grant the ``locked`` status until every checkpoint validates.
   22: Until then the gate refuses to PASS smokes that consume the lock.
   23: """
   24: 
   25: from __future__ import annotations
   26: 
   27: import hashlib
   28: import subprocess
   29: import sys
   30: from pathlib import Path
   31: 
   32: import yaml  # type: ignore[import-not-found]
   33: 
   34: 
   35: class LockMismatch(Exception):
   36:     """Raised when the runtime codebase does not honor the architecture lock."""
   37: 
   38: 
   39: REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent.parent
   40: LOCK_PATH = REPO_ROOT / "config" / "architecture" / "polaris_runtime_lock.yaml"
   41: CANONICAL_PIN_PATH = REPO_ROOT / "docs" / "canonical_pin.txt"
   42: 
   43: 
   44: def load_lock() -> dict:
   45:     """Load and parse the runtime lock YAML. Raises if missing/malformed."""
   46:     if not LOCK_PATH.exists():
   47:         raise LockMismatch(f"architecture lock missing: {LOCK_PATH}")
   48:     return yaml.safe_load(LOCK_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
   49: 
   50: 
   51: def sha256_of(path: Path) -> str:
   52:     """SHA256 of a file's contents, hex digest."""
   53:     h = hashlib.sha256()
   54:     h.update(path.read_bytes())
   55:     return h.hexdigest()
   56: 
   57: 
   58: def _git_tracked(rel_path: str) -> bool:
   59:     """True iff rel_path is tracked by git in the repo at REPO_ROOT."""
   60:     try:
   61:         out = subprocess.run(
   62:             ["git", "ls-files", "--error-unmatch", rel_path],
   63:             cwd=REPO_ROOT, capture_output=True, text=True,
   64:         )
   65:         return out.returncode == 0
   66:     except Exception:
   67:         return False
   68: 
   69: 
   70: def verify_lock_against_code() -> dict:
   71:     """Compare lock declarations against runtime code defaults + family registry + envs.
   72: 
   73:     Returns a dict of {role: {ok: bool, mismatches: [...]}}. Raises LockMismatch
   74:     only if any role's defaults diverge in a way that breaks the architecture.
   75:     Family-registry coverage is checked separately (a missing family entry =
   76:     hard fail because family-segregation cannot validate the role).
   77:     """
   78:     lock = load_lock()
   79:     results: dict = {}
   80: 
   81:     # Import the family registry lazily so this module stays import-safe at boot.
   82:     from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import _FAMILY_PREFIXES
   83: 
   84:     declared_families = {role: spec["family"] for role, spec in lock["required_roles"].items()}
   85:     missing_in_registry = [f for f in declared_families.values() if f not in _FAMILY_PREFIXES]
   86:     if missing_in_registry:
   87:         raise LockMismatch(
   88:             f"family registry lacks declared families {missing_in_registry!r}; "
   89:             f"add to src/polaris_graph/llm/openrouter_client.py:_FAMILY_PREFIXES"
   90:         )
   91: 
   92:     # Family policy: all_distinct
   93:     if lock.get("family_policy", {}).get("default_policy") == "all_distinct":
   94:         seen: dict[str, str] = {}
   95:         for role, fam in declared_families.items():
   96:             if fam in seen:
   97:                 raise LockMismatch(
   98:                     f"family policy violation: role {role!r} and role {seen[fam]!r} "
   99:                     f"share family {fam!r}; allowed_collisions is empty"
  100:                 )
  101:             seen[fam] = role
  102: 
  103:     # Slug check: each role's lock model_slug must equal its code default.
  104:     # Import lazily so this module stays import-safe at boot.
  105:     from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import (
  106:         PG_GENERATOR_MODEL,
  107:         PG_JUDGE_MODEL,
  108:         PG_MIRROR_MODEL,
  109:         PG_SENTINEL_MODEL,
  110:     )
  111: 
  112:     role_to_code_default = {
  113:         "generator": PG_GENERATOR_MODEL,
  114:         "mirror": PG_MIRROR_MODEL,
  115:         "sentinel": PG_SENTINEL_MODEL,
  116:         "judge": PG_JUDGE_MODEL,
  117:     }
  118: 
  119:     for role, spec in lock["required_roles"].items():
  120:         code_default = role_to_code_default.get(role)
  121:         if code_default is None:
  122:             # No code-default constant for this role; skip the slug assertion.
  123:             continue
  124:         declared = spec["model_slug"]
  125:         if declared != code_default:
  126:             raise LockMismatch(
  127:                 f"role {role!r} lock model_slug {declared!r} does not match "
  128:                 f"code default {code_default!r}; reconcile "
  129:                 f"config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml with "
  130:                 f"src/polaris_graph/llm/openrouter_client.py"
  131:             )
  132: 
  133:     for role, spec in lock["required_roles"].items():
  134:         results[role] = {
  135:             "ok": True,
  136:             "declared_model": spec["model_slug"],
  137:             "declared_family": spec["family"],
  138:             "mismatches": [],
  139:         }
  140: 
  141:     return results
  142: 
  143: 
  144: def check_propagation_manifest() -> dict:
  145:     """Run every propagation checkpoint. Returns {checkpoint: bool}.
  146: 
  147:     The lock cannot graduate from codex_approved_pending_operator_signature to
  148:     locked until every checkpoint is True. Caller decides what to do with the
  149:     result (CI gate, pre-merge check, etc.)
  150:     """
  151:     lock = load_lock()
  152:     checkpoints = {
  153:         "this_file_committed": _git_tracked("config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml"),
  154:         "source_doc_committed": _git_tracked(lock["source_doc"]),
  155:         "canonical_pin_includes_this_file": False,
  156:         "code_defaults_match": False,
  157:         "tests_pass": False,  # CI-set; not checked here
  158:     }
  159: 
  160:     if CANONICAL_PIN_PATH.exists():
  161:         pin_content = CANONICAL_PIN_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
  162:         checkpoints["canonical_pin_includes_this_file"] = "config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml" in pin_content
  163: 
  164:     try:
  165:         verify_lock_against_code()
  166:         checkpoints["code_defaults_match"] = True
  167:     except LockMismatch:
  168:         pass
  169: 
  170:     return checkpoints
  171: 
  172: 
  173: def report(stream=sys.stdout) -> int:
  174:     """Print a human-readable report. Exit-code semantics: 0 = all green; non-zero otherwise."""
  175:     try:
  176:         lock = load_lock()
  177:     except LockMismatch as exc:
  178:         print(f"FATAL: {exc}", file=stream)
  179:         return 2
  180: 
  181:     print(f"POLARIS architecture lock — {LOCK_PATH}", file=stream)
  182:     print(f"  status: {lock.get('status')}", file=stream)
  183:     print(f"  source_doc: {lock.get('source_doc')}", file=stream)
  184:     print(f"  codex_verdict: {lock.get('codex_verdict')}", file=stream)
  185:     print("", file=stream)
  186: 
  187:     print("Required roles:", file=stream)
  188:     for role, spec in lock["required_roles"].items():
  189:         print(f"  {role}: {spec['model_slug']} (family={spec['family']}, license={spec['license']})", file=stream)
  190:     print("", file=stream)
  191: 
  192:     try:
  193:         verify_lock_against_code()
  194:         print("Code-defaults verification: OK", file=stream)
  195:     except LockMismatch as exc:
  196:         print(f"Code-defaults verification: FAIL — {exc}", file=stream)
  197:         return 1
  198: 
  199:     checkpoints = check_propagation_manifest()
  200:     print("", file=stream)
  201:     print("Propagation manifest:", file=stream)
  202:     all_ok = True
  203:     for name, ok in checkpoints.items():
  204:         marker = "OK" if ok else "PENDING"
  205:         print(f"  [{marker}] {name}", file=stream)
  206:         if not ok:
  207:             all_ok = False
  208: 
  209:     print("", file=stream)
  210:     if all_ok and lock.get("status") == "codex_approved_pending_operator_signature":
  211:         print("ALL CHECKPOINTS PASS — lock can be promoted to status: locked", file=stream)
  212:         return 0
  213:     elif all_ok and lock.get("status") == "locked":
  214:         print("Lock is LOCKED and all checkpoints validate.", file=stream)
  215:         return 0
  216:     else:
  217:         print("Lock NOT yet promotable; complete missing checkpoints.", file=stream)
  218:         return 1
  219: 
  220: 
  221: def verify_consistency(stream=sys.stdout) -> int:
  222:     """Status-independent consistency gate.
  223: 
  224:     Returns 0 when ALL of the following hold, REGARDLESS of the lock's
  225:     ``status`` field or the propagation ``tests_pass`` checkpoint:
  226:       - the lock YAML loads
  227:       - every declared family is registered in _FAMILY_PREFIXES
  228:       - family_policy (all_distinct) holds
  229:       - code defaults match the lock model_slugs
  230:       - canonical_pin.txt includes the lock file path
  231: 
  232:     The first four are covered by verify_lock_against_code(); the last is a
  233:     substring presence check on canonical_pin.txt. This deliberately does NOT
  234:     route through check_propagation_manifest() (which hardwires tests_pass=False
  235:     and git-tracked checks). Returns 0 on full consistency, 1 on any mismatch.
  236:     """
  237:     try:
  238:         verify_lock_against_code()
  239:     except LockMismatch as exc:
  240:         print(f"Consistency: FAIL — {exc}", file=stream)
  241:         return 1
  242: 
  243:     if not CANONICAL_PIN_PATH.exists():
  244:         print(
  245:             f"Consistency: FAIL — canonical pin missing: {CANONICAL_PIN_PATH}",
  246:             file=stream,
  247:         )
  248:         return 1
  249: 
  250:     pin_content = CANONICAL_PIN_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
  251:     if "config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml" not in pin_content:
  252:         print(
  253:             "Consistency: FAIL — canonical_pin.txt does not include the lock file",
  254:             file=stream,
  255:         )
  256:         return 1
  257: 
  258:     print("Consistency: OK — families registered, family_policy holds, "
  259:           "code defaults match lock, canonical_pin includes lock file", file=stream)
  260:     return 0
